732[{"@context":"http://schema.org","@type":"NewsArticle","articleBody":"*In* [*Here We Are*](https://www.bonappetit.com/tag/here-we-are)*, artist **Martine Thompson** explores what it means to care for oneself in a world that doesn’t make it so easy. Up next, a guide to building a joy toolbox to give yourself a midwinter boost. Read on, but don’t forget to check out her* [*winter playlist*](https://open.spotify.com/playlist/4YJg8y2m31f24O1Lp5ia1g) *too.*\n\nThis was one long, hellish year with some highs, yes, but also some very painful lows. I don’t consider myself religious, but truly there were some moments when I had to just stop, lie down, play **Marvin Sapp**’s “[Never Would’ve Made It](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7JXFg5KEoXg),” and just breathe. There’s been a lot to process: the 2020 election season; an unprecedented worldwide pandemic; **George Floyd**’s murder and the global centuries-long abuse of Black people igniting uprisings across the nation, followed by the countless performative gestures that dodged any real heavy lifting and postured as meaningful solidarity. Like I said, it’s been a *looong* year.\n\nWinter is around the corner and with heightened feelings of *meh* accompanying the seasonal change, I’ve been thinking about [joy toolboxes](https://thechalkboardmag.com/joy-toolbox) and how helpful it is to have a go-to stock of activities and practices that make you feel good. There are so many heartaches, tragedies, and fucked-up normalities that can unexpectedly knock the wind out of us. So many plot twists in life that nudge us to reevaluate and reimagine what we understand as self-care. While there’s obviously no one-size-fits-all quick fix for tough times or feeling blue, and the short-lived thrill of buying something that comes and goes, I do think it’s worthwhile to find ways to add more joy and tranquility into the day-to-day. From soothing lighting that puts me in my zone to perspective shifts that have helped me embrace the fluidity of life more, here are five things in my wellness toolbox that may inspire your own.\n\n#### Go on a new food adventure\nWith the food industry [still in dire need of support](https://www.bonappetit.com/story/food-businesses-covid-19){: target=\"_blank\"} and the same monotonous routine filling many of our quarantine days, now is an especially good time to treat ourselves to takeout from that restaurant or cool new pop-up bookmarked on our Instagrams. You know, the one that evoked an “[I’ve gotta try that\\!](https://www.instagram.com/p/CHtGMmUFeGK/?igshid=1f66t8l6yswk6)” as soon as it crossed your feed. This was exactly the case when I came across Jamaican chef, model, creative technopreneur, and [multimedia storyteller](https://thatmiddlechild.com/builtnotbought#:~:text=BUILT%2520NOT%2520BOUGHT-,ABOUT,of%2520Los%2520Angeles%2520at%2520large.) **Jazzy Harvey** serving a revolving menu of Jamaican fusion takeout in Los Angeles’s Crenshaw District. The [Anjahles Jamaican x LA Fusion](https://www.instagram.com/anjahles) founder and head chef’s current menu offers a remixed selection of Caribbean classics: oxtail mac ’n’ cheese, vegan jerk gumbo, candied “dark and lovely” plantain.\n\nBeyond a highly Instagrammable good meal, it feels great to support a small business that prioritizes community and is intentional about giving back, like bringing music and 300-plus free meals to Leimert Park alongside [**chef Hugh Augustine**](https://www.bonappetit.com/story/hughs-hot-bowls){: target=\"_blank\"}, **chef Marcus Yaw**, **chef James B**, and **DJ Coly Cole** for a [Community Friendsgiving](https://www.instagram.com/tv/CIRzzohAke2/?igshid=yujk6p79adbm){: target=\"_blank\"} last month. Regardless of where you live, take this winter as an opportunity to make a mini mission around intentionally supporting food businesses, and if you’re around the Crenshaw neighborhood or L.A. County, add Anjahles to your list (and stay tuned for its [upcoming pop-ups](https://www.instagram.com/p/CI3q14pg3oW/?igshid=1x9swmk0kjwjl){: target=\"_blank\"} around the city and [holiday catering menu](https://www.instagram.com/p/CI8548NANP2/?igshid=pyo0s60209d9){: rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\"}).\n\n#### Commit to making your space a happy place\nMaking your space feel like a cozy slice of paradise goes a long way toward combating winter blues. For me, that looks like regularly having fresh flowers around the house, treating myself to [fun glassware](https://comingsoonnewyork.com/products/gradient-glass) that gets me daydreaming about post-quarantine get-togethers, and always having candles on deck. Whether I’m relaxing or working, being in a setting with dim lighting coming only from the glow of candles sets the perfect mood. My current favorites are the coconut shell soy candles from [Isle of Wax](https://isleofwax.com/), a candle line launched by Saint Lucia native **Danielle Privat** to celebrate smells of the Caribbean that I discovered on [@blackownedeverything](https://www.instagram.com/blackownedeverything), an Instagram highlighting Black-owned businesses created by stylist **Zerina Akers**. The Saint Lucia candle filled my room with the most amazing fruity-meets-fresh-laundry smell before even being lit. Opening my package—filled with a flurry of sweet scents, vibrant blue stuffing, and a thoughtful handwritten note—felt like Christmas.\n\n#### Have your therapy/wellness resources up-to-date\nFinding a new therapist—or other wellness support—can be such a daunting experience, and if you’re seeking a care provider who shares certain identity intersections with you, like also being a Black woman and/or trans, multiply that by 1,000. I find it super helpful to have a few go-to directories in the toolbox to make the search less of a headache when the need arises. Here are some resources to start with: [Queer Healers](https://queerhealers.com/), whose directory of queer practitioners include herbalists, tarot readers, astrologists, sex therapists, birth/abortion/death doulas, and more. [Therapy for Black Girls](https://therapyforblackgirls.com/) focuses on connecting Black women with local Black women therapists, and also offers a [wellness blog](https://therapyforblackgirls.com/blog/) and a [mental health podcast](https://therapyforblackgirls.com/podcast/) led by psychologist, speaker, and founder **Dr. Joy Harden Bradford**. [Black Female Therapists](https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/directory) offers a directory of Black women therapists, including a listing of the type of care they specialize in (e.g., anxiety, depression, body image, LGBTQIA\\+ identity), a [podcast](https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/podcast), and a mental health blog. You can also check out [six other mental health resources](https://www.bonappetit.com/story/virtual-mental-health-resources) offering virtual support to Black people—and I’m adding Lauryn Hill’s live album [*Lauryn Hill Unplugged No. 2.0*](https://open.spotify.com/album/22tn8fUpD1lurSga9yuqhM) because no one can tell me listening to it in the car doesn’t have special healing properties.\n\n#### Try a new type of weed (if you’re into that)\nIn hindsight, chilling in bed on my phone after trying Canndescent’s [“charge” joint](https://www.canndescent.com/pre-rolls) feels like a missed opportunity considering how much of an enjoyable body/mind high it provided. Maybe I should’ve had a station ready with snacks, coloring books, art activities, and tender/funny videos? My thoughts once the high started to wane were basically, Wow, well, I guess I’m going to have to be a grown-up and start investing in quality weed now. It was easily the best high I’ve experienced from a pre-rolled joint. Canndescent offers (limited-edition) [holiday joints](https://www.iheartjane.com/embed/stores/2219/products/202311/canndescent-cheer?utm_source=copy&utm_medium=organic_social&utm_campaign=product_share&utm_content=2219?blockScrollToTop) too\\! If you’re looking to broaden your weed toolbox, consider trying out [Papa & Barkley’s THC body oil](https://papaandbarkley.com/product/releaf-body-oil/) for pain and tension relief. And if exploring vaginal cannabis products is of interest, [Quim’s everyday CBD (or THC) oil](https://itsquim.com/product/happy-clam/) can be used for everything from menstruation relief to post-shower TLC.\n\n#### Embrace optimism and uncertainty as an act of wellness\nLately, I’ve been opening up more to the idea that positive occurrences and opportunities, as well as the roads leading to them, may not manifest in the way I envisioned in my head—and maybe that’s okay. I’ve also decided to give leaning into positive *what-ifs* a go. *What if* this isn’t working out because I’m being redirected to something that’s more aligned with who I am and what I want? *What if* there’s no need to chase or frantically grasp and that certain roadblocks are blessings in disguise? *What if* the right things, the right people, and all of the good shit will flow into your life, and the task isn’t to chase or mourn or be swallowed up by shame, but rather to learn, explore, heal, and evolve into the best *most you* version of yourself? *What if* “all of the good shit” looks nothing like you ever imagined? *What if* it’s going to be okay, even if it doesn’t feel like it, even if you can’t see or feel that light at the end of the tunnel right now? If you believed that, what would you do next? That’s the space I’ve been exploring lately, and it’s a refreshing change of pace.\n\n","articleSection":"healthyish","author":[{"@type":"Person","name":"Martine 1004<h1 class="content-header__row content-header__hed" data-testid="ContentHeaderHed">

1005These 5 Things in My “Joy Toolbox” Are Getting Me Through Winter</h1>

1006<span class="content-header__row content-header__secondary-rule">

1149<div class="BaseWrap-sc-TURhJ BodyWrapper-ctnerm eTiIvU cKFUKx body grid--item body__container article__body grid-layout__content" data-journey-hook="client-content">

1150<div class="body__inner-container">

1151<p>

1152<em>

1153In</em>

1154 <a href="https://www.bonappetit.com/tag/here-we-are">

1155<em>

1156Here We Are</em>

1157</a>

1158<em>

1159, artist <strong>

1160Martine Thompson</strong>

1161 explores what it means to care for oneself in a world that doesn’t make it so easy. Up next, a guide to building a joy toolbox to give yourself a midwinter boost. Read on, but don’t forget to check out her</em>

1162 <a data-offer-url="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/4YJg8y2m31f24O1Lp5ia1g" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://open.spotify.com/playlist/4YJg8y2m31f24O1Lp5ia1g&quot;}" href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/4YJg8y2m31f24O1Lp5ia1g" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1163<em>

1164winter playlist</em>

1165</a>

1166 <em>

1167too.</em>

1168</p>

1169<p>

1170This was one long, hellish year with some highs, yes, but also some very painful lows. I don’t consider myself religious, but truly there were some moments when I had to just stop, lie down, play <strong>

1171Marvin Sapp</strong>

1172’s “<a data-offer-url="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7JXFg5KEoXg" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7JXFg5KEoXg&quot;}" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7JXFg5KEoXg" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1173Never Would’ve Made It</a>

1174,” and just breathe. There’s been a lot to process: the 2020 election season; an unprecedented worldwide pandemic; <strong>

1175George Floyd</strong>

1176’s murder and the global centuries-long abuse of Black people igniting uprisings across the nation, followed by the countless performative gestures that dodged any real heavy lifting and postured as meaningful solidarity. Like I said, it’s been a <em>

1177looong</em>

1178 year.</p>

1179<p>

1180Winter is around the corner and with heightened feelings of <em>

1181meh</em>

1182 accompanying the seasonal change, I’ve been thinking about <a data-offer-url="https://thechalkboardmag.com/joy-toolbox" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://thechalkboardmag.com/joy-toolbox&quot;}" href="https://thechalkboardmag.com/joy-toolbox" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1183joy toolboxes</a>

1184 and how helpful it is to have a go-to stock of activities and practices that make you feel good. There are so many heartaches, tragedies, and fucked-up normalities that can unexpectedly knock the wind out of us. So many plot twists in life that nudge us to reevaluate and reimagine what we understand as self-care. While there’s obviously no one-size-fits-all quick fix for tough times or feeling blue, and the short-lived thrill of buying something that comes and goes, I do think it’s worthwhile to find ways to add more joy and tranquility into the day-to-day. From soothing lighting that puts me in my zone to perspective shifts that have helped me embrace the fluidity of life more, here are five things in my wellness toolbox that may inspire your own.</p>

1185<div role="heading" aria-level="4" class="heading-h4">

1186Go on a new food adventure</div>

1187<p>

1188With the food industry <a href="https://www.bonappetit.com/story/food-businesses-covid-19" target="_blank">

1189still in dire need of support</a>

1190 and the same monotonous routine filling many of our quarantine days, now is an especially good time to treat ourselves to takeout from that restaurant or cool new pop-up bookmarked on our Instagrams. You know, the one that evoked an “<a data-offer-url="https://www.instagram.com/p/CHtGMmUFeGK/?igshid=1f66t8l6yswk6" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.instagram.com/p/CHtGMmUFeGK/?igshid=1f66t8l6yswk6&quot;}" href="https://www.instagram.com/p/CHtGMmUFeGK/?igshid=1f66t8l6yswk6" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1191I’ve gotta try that!</a>

1192” as soon as it crossed your feed. This was exactly the case when I came across Jamaican chef, model, creative technopreneur, and <a data-offer-url="https://thatmiddlechild.com/builtnotbought#:~:text=BUILT%2520NOT%2520BOUGHT-,ABOUT,of%2520Los%2520Angeles%2520at%2520large." class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://thatmiddlechild.com/builtnotbought#:~:text=BUILT%2520NOT%2520BOUGHT-,ABOUT,of%2520Los%2520Angeles%2520at%2520large.&quot;}" href="https://thatmiddlechild.com/builtnotbought#:~:text=BUILT%2520NOT%2520BOUGHT-,ABOUT,of%2520Los%2520Angeles%2520at%2520large." rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1193multimedia storyteller</a>

1194 <strong>

1195Jazzy Harvey</strong>

1196 serving a revolving menu of Jamaican fusion takeout in Los Angeles’s Crenshaw District. The <a data-offer-url="https://www.instagram.com/anjahles" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.instagram.com/anjahles&quot;}" href="https://www.instagram.com/anjahles" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1197Anjahles Jamaican x LA Fusion</a>

1198 founder and head chef’s current menu offers a remixed selection of Caribbean classics: oxtail mac ’n’ cheese, vegan jerk gumbo, candied “dark and lovely” plantain.</p>

1199<div class="Container-imGeBO ftlPuP">

1200</div>

1201<p>

1202Beyond a highly Instagrammable good meal, it feels great to support a small business that prioritizes community and is intentional about giving back, like bringing music and 300-plus free meals to Leimert Park alongside <a href="https://www.bonappetit.com/story/hughs-hot-bowls" target="_blank">

1203<strong>

1204chef Hugh Augustine</strong>

1205</a>

1206, <strong>

1207chef Marcus Yaw</strong>

1208, <strong>

1209chef James B</strong>

1210, and <strong>

1211DJ Coly Cole</strong>

1212 for a <a data-offer-url="https://www.instagram.com/tv/CIRzzohAke2/?igshid=yujk6p79adbm" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.instagram.com/tv/CIRzzohAke2/?igshid=yujk6p79adbm&quot;}" href="https://www.instagram.com/tv/CIRzzohAke2/?igshid=yujk6p79adbm" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1213Community Friendsgiving</a>

1214 last month. Regardless of where you live, take this winter as an opportunity to make a mini mission around intentionally supporting food businesses, and if you’re around the Crenshaw neighborhood or L.A. County, add Anjahles to your list (and stay tuned for its <a data-offer-url="https://www.instagram.com/p/CI3q14pg3oW/?igshid=1x9swmk0kjwjl" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.instagram.com/p/CI3q14pg3oW/?igshid=1x9swmk0kjwjl&quot;}" href="https://www.instagram.com/p/CI3q14pg3oW/?igshid=1x9swmk0kjwjl" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1215upcoming pop-ups</a>

1216 around the city and <a data-offer-url="https://www.instagram.com/p/CI8548NANP2/?igshid=pyo0s60209d9" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.instagram.com/p/CI8548NANP2/?igshid=pyo0s60209d9&quot;}" href="https://www.instagram.com/p/CI8548NANP2/?igshid=pyo0s60209d9" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">

1217holiday catering menu</a>

1218).</p>

1219<div role="heading" aria-level="4" class="heading-h4">

1220Commit to making your space a happy place</div>

1221<p>

1222Making your space feel like a cozy slice of paradise goes a long way toward combating winter blues. For me, that looks like regularly having fresh flowers around the house, treating myself to <a data-offer-url="https://comingsoonnewyork.com/products/gradient-glass" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://comingsoonnewyork.com/products/gradient-glass&quot;}" href="https://comingsoonnewyork.com/products/gradient-glass" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1223fun glassware</a>

1224 that gets me daydreaming about post-quarantine get-togethers, and always having candles on deck. Whether I’m relaxing or working, being in a setting with dim lighting coming only from the glow of candles sets the perfect mood. My current favorites are the coconut shell soy candles from <a data-offer-url="https://isleofwax.com/" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://isleofwax.com/&quot;}" href="https://isleofwax.com/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1225Isle of Wax</a>

1226, a candle line launched by Saint Lucia native <strong>

1227Danielle Privat</strong>

1228 to celebrate smells of the Caribbean that I discovered on <a data-offer-url="https://www.instagram.com/blackownedeverything" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.instagram.com/blackownedeverything&quot;}" href="https://www.instagram.com/blackownedeverything" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1229@blackownedeverything</a>

1230, an Instagram highlighting Black-owned businesses created by stylist <strong>

1231Zerina Akers</strong>

1232. The Saint Lucia candle filled my room with the most amazing fruity-meets-fresh-laundry smell before even being lit. Opening my package—filled with a flurry of sweet scents, vibrant blue stuffing, and a thoughtful handwritten note—felt like Christmas.</p>

1233<div role="heading" aria-level="4" class="heading-h4">

1234Have your therapy/wellness resources up-to-date</div>

1235<p>

1236Finding a new therapist—or other wellness support—can be such a daunting experience, and if you’re seeking a care provider who shares certain identity intersections with you, like also being a Black woman and/or trans, multiply that by 1,000. I find it super helpful to have a few go-to directories in the toolbox to make the search less of a headache when the need arises. Here are some resources to start with: <a data-offer-url="https://queerhealers.com/" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://queerhealers.com/&quot;}" href="https://queerhealers.com/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1237Queer Healers</a>

1238, whose directory of queer practitioners include herbalists, tarot readers, astrologists, sex therapists, birth/abortion/death doulas, and more. <a data-offer-url="https://therapyforblackgirls.com/" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://therapyforblackgirls.com/&quot;}" href="https://therapyforblackgirls.com/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1239Therapy for Black Girls</a>

1240 focuses on connecting Black women with local Black women therapists, and also offers a <a data-offer-url="https://therapyforblackgirls.com/blog/" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://therapyforblackgirls.com/blog/&quot;}" href="https://therapyforblackgirls.com/blog/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1241wellness blog</a>

1242 and a <a data-offer-url="https://therapyforblackgirls.com/podcast/" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://therapyforblackgirls.com/podcast/&quot;}" href="https://therapyforblackgirls.com/podcast/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1243mental health podcast</a>

1244 led by psychologist, speaker, and founder <strong>

1245Dr. Joy Harden Bradford</strong>

1246. <a data-offer-url="https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/directory" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/directory&quot;}" href="https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/directory" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1247Black Female Therapists</a>

1248 offers a directory of Black women therapists, including a listing of the type of care they specialize in (e.g., anxiety, depression, body image, LGBTQIA+ identity), a <a data-offer-url="https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/podcast" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/podcast&quot;}" href="https://www.blackfemaletherapists.com/podcast" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1249podcast</a>

1250, and a mental health blog. You can also check out <a href="https://www.bonappetit.com/story/virtual-mental-health-resources">

1251six other mental health resources</a>

1252 offering virtual support to Black people—and I’m adding Lauryn Hill’s live album <a data-offer-url="https://open.spotify.com/album/22tn8fUpD1lurSga9yuqhM" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://open.spotify.com/album/22tn8fUpD1lurSga9yuqhM&quot;}" href="https://open.spotify.com/album/22tn8fUpD1lurSga9yuqhM" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1253<em>

1254Lauryn Hill Unplugged No. 2.0</em>

1255</a>

1256 because no one can tell me listening to it in the car doesn’t have special healing properties.</p>

1257<div role="heading" aria-level="4" class="heading-h4">

1258Try a new type of weed (if you’re into that)</div>

1259<p>

1260In hindsight, chilling in bed on my phone after trying Canndescent’s <a data-offer-url="https://www.canndescent.com/pre-rolls" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.canndescent.com/pre-rolls&quot;}" href="https://www.canndescent.com/pre-rolls" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1261“charge” joint</a>

1262 feels like a missed opportunity considering how much of an enjoyable body/mind high it provided. Maybe I should’ve had a station ready with snacks, coloring books, art activities, and tender/funny videos? My thoughts once the high started to wane were basically, Wow, well, I guess I’m going to have to be a grown-up and start investing in quality weed now. It was easily the best high I’ve experienced from a pre-rolled joint. Canndescent offers (limited-edition) <a data-offer-url="https://www.iheartjane.com/embed/stores/2219/products/202311/canndescent-cheer?utm_source=copy&amp;utm_medium=organic_social&amp;utm_campaign=product_share&amp;utm_content=2219?blockScrollToTop" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://www.iheartjane.com/embed/stores/2219/products/202311/canndescent-cheer?utm_source=copy&amp;utm_medium=organic_social&amp;utm_campaign=product_share&amp;utm_content=2219?blockScrollToTop&quot;}" href="https://www.iheartjane.com/embed/stores/2219/products/202311/canndescent-cheer?utm_source=copy&amp;utm_medium=organic_social&amp;utm_campaign=product_share&amp;utm_content=2219?blockScrollToTop" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1263holiday joints</a>

1264 too! If you’re looking to broaden your weed toolbox, consider trying out <a data-offer-url="https://papaandbarkley.com/product/releaf-body-oil/" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://papaandbarkley.com/product/releaf-body-oil/&quot;}" href="https://papaandbarkley.com/product/releaf-body-oil/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1265Papa &amp; Barkley’s THC body oil</a>

1266 for pain and tension relief. And if exploring vaginal cannabis products is of interest, <a data-offer-url="https://itsquim.com/product/happy-clam/" class="external-link" data-event-click="{&quot;element&quot;:&quot;ExternalLink&quot;,&quot;outgoingURL&quot;:&quot;https://itsquim.com/product/happy-clam/&quot;}" href="https://itsquim.com/product/happy-clam/" rel="nofollow noopener" target="_blank">

1267Quim’s everyday CBD (or THC) oil</a>

1268 can be used for everything from menstruation relief to post-shower TLC.</p>

1269<div role="heading" aria-level="4" class="heading-h4">

1270Embrace optimism and uncertainty as an act of wellness</div>

1271<p>

1272Lately, I’ve been opening up more to the idea that positive occurrences and opportunities, as well as the roads leading to them, may not manifest in the way I envisioned in my head—and maybe that’s okay. I’ve also decided to give leaning into positive <em>

1273what-ifs</em>

1274 a go. <em>

1275What if</em>

1276 this isn’t working out because I’m being redirected to something that’s more aligned with who I am and what I want? <em>

1277What if</em>

1278 there’s no need to chase or frantically grasp and that certain roadblocks are blessings in disguise? <em>

1279What if</em>

1280 the right things, the right people, and all of the good shit will flow into your life, and the task isn’t to chase or mourn or be swallowed up by shame, but rather to learn, explore, heal, and evolve into the best <em>

1281most you</em>

1282 version of yourself? <em>

1283What if</em>

1284 “all of the good shit” looks nothing like you ever imagined? <em>

1285What if</em>

1286 it’s going to be okay, even if it doesn’t feel like it, even if you can’t see or feel that light at the end of the tunnel right now? If you believed that, what would you do next? That’s the space I’ve been exploring lately, and it’s a refreshing change of pace.</p>

winter.","head.social.opinion":"false","head.jsonld":[{"@context":"http:\u002F\u002Fschema.org","@type":"NewsArticle","articleBody":"*In* [*Here We Are*](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bonappetit.com\u002Ftag\u002Fhere-we-are)*, artist **Martine Thompson** explores what it means to care for oneself in a world that doesn’t make it so easy. Up next, a guide to building a joy toolbox to give yourself a midwinter boost. Read on, but don’t forget to check out her* [*winter playlist*](https:\u002F\u002Fopen.spotify.com\u002Fplaylist\u002F4YJg8y2m31f24O1Lp5ia1g) *too.*\n\nThis was one long, hellish year with some highs, yes, but also some very painful lows. I don’t consider myself religious, but truly there were some moments when I had to just stop, lie down, play **Marvin Sapp**’s “[Never Would’ve Made It](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=7JXFg5KEoXg),” and just breathe. There’s been a lot to process: the 2020 election season; an unprecedented worldwide pandemic; **George Floyd**’s murder and the global centuries-long abuse of Black people igniting uprisings across the nation, followed by the countless performative gestures that dodged any real heavy lifting and postured as meaningful solidarity. Like I said, it’s been a *looong* year.\n\nWinter is around the corner and with heightened feelings of *meh* accompanying the seasonal change, I’ve been thinking about [joy toolboxes](https:\u002F\u002Fthechalkboardmag.com\u002Fjoy-toolbox) and how helpful it is to have a go-to stock of activities and practices that make you feel good. There are so many heartaches, tragedies, and fucked-up normalities that can unexpectedly knock the wind out of us. So many plot twists in life that nudge us to reevaluate and reimagine what we understand as self-care. While there’s obviously no one-size-fits-all quick fix for tough times or feeling blue, and the short-lived thrill of buying something that comes and goes, I do think it’s worthwhile to find ways to add more joy and tranquility into the day-to-day. From soothing lighting that puts me in my zone to perspective shifts that have helped me embrace the fluidity of life more, here are five things in my wellness toolbox that may inspire your own.\n\n#### Go on a new food adventure\nWith the food industry [still in dire need of support](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bonappetit.com\u002Fstory\u002Ffood-businesses-covid-19){: target=\"_blank\"} and the same monotonous routine filling many of our quarantine days, now is an especially good time to treat ourselves to takeout from that restaurant or cool new pop-up bookmarked on our Instagrams. You know, the one that evoked an “[I’ve gotta try that\\!](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.instagram.com\u002Fp\u002FCHtGMmUFeGK\u002F?igshid=1f66t8l6yswk6)” as soon as it crossed your feed. This was exactly the case when I came across Jamaican chef, model, creative technopreneur, and [multimedia storyteller](https:\u002F\u002Fthatmiddlechild.com\u002Fbuiltnotbought#:~:text=BUILT%2520NOT%2520BOUGHT-,ABOUT,of%2520Los%2520Angeles%2520at%2520large.) **Jazzy Harvey** serving a revolving menu of Jamaican fusion takeout in Los Angeles’s Crenshaw District. The [Anjahles Jamaican x LA Fusion](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.instagram.com\u002Fanjahles) founder and head chef’s current menu offers a remixed selection of Caribbean classics: oxtail mac ’n’ cheese, vegan jerk gumbo, candied “dark and lovely” plantain.\n\nBeyond a highly Instagrammable good meal, it feels great to support a small business that prioritizes community and is intentional about giving back, like bringing music and 300-plus free meals to Leimert Park alongside [**chef Hugh Augustine**](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bonappetit.com\u002Fstory\u002Fhughs-hot-bowls){: target=\"_blank\"}, **chef Marcus Yaw**, **chef James B**, and **DJ Coly Cole** for a [Community Friendsgiving](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.instagram.com\u002Ftv\u002FCIRzzohAke2\u002F?igshid=yujk6p79adbm){: target=\"_blank\"} last month. Regardless of where you live, take this winter as an opportunity to make a mini mission around intentionally supporting food businesses, and if you’re around the Crenshaw neighborhood or L.A. County, add Anjahles to your list (and stay tuned for its [upcoming pop-ups](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.instagram.com\u002Fp\u002FCI3q14pg3oW\u002F?igshid=1x9swmk0kjwjl){: target=\"_blank\"} around the city and [holiday catering menu](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.instagram.com\u002Fp\u002FCI8548NANP2\u002F?igshid=pyo0s60209d9){: rel=\"nofollow\" target=\"_blank\"}).\n\n#### Commit to making your space a happy place\nMaking your space feel like a cozy slice of paradise goes a long way toward combating winter blues. For me, that looks like regularly having fresh flowers around the house, treating myself to [fun glassware](https:\u002F\u002Fcomingsoonnewyork.com\u002Fproducts\u002Fgradient-glass) that gets me daydreaming about post-quarantine get-togethers, and always having candles on deck. Whether I’m relaxing or working, being in a setting with dim lighting coming only from the glow of candles sets the perfect mood. My current favorites are the coconut shell soy candles from [Isle of Wax](https:\u002F\u002Fisleofwax.com\u002F), a candle line launched by Saint Lucia native **Danielle Privat** to celebrate smells of the Caribbean that I discovered on [@blackownedeverything](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.instagram.com\u002Fblackownedeverything), an Instagram highlighting Black-owned businesses created by stylist **Zerina Akers**. The Saint Lucia candle filled my room with the most amazing fruity-meets-fresh-laundry smell before even being lit. Opening my package—filled with a flurry of sweet scents, vibrant blue stuffing, and a thoughtful handwritten note—felt like Christmas.\n\n#### Have your therapy\u002Fwellness resources up-to-date\nFinding a new therapist—or other wellness support—can be such a daunting experience, and if you’re seeking a care provider who shares certain identity intersections with you, like also being a Black woman and\u002For trans, multiply that by 1,000. I find it super helpful to have a few go-to directories in the toolbox to make the search less of a headache when the need arises. Here are some resources to start with: [Queer Healers](https:\u002F\u002Fqueerhealers.com\u002F), whose directory of queer practitioners include herbalists, tarot readers, astrologists, sex therapists, birth\u002Fabortion\u002Fdeath doulas, and more. [Therapy for Black Girls](https:\u002F\u002Ftherapyforblackgirls.com\u002F) focuses on connecting Black women with local Black women therapists, and also offers a [wellness blog](https:\u002F\u002Ftherapyforblackgirls.com\u002Fblog\u002F) and a [mental health podcast](https:\u002F\u002Ftherapyforblackgirls.com\u002Fpodcast\u002F) led by psychologist, speaker, and founder **Dr. Joy Harden Bradford**. [Black Female Therapists](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.blackfemaletherapists.com\u002Fdirectory) offers a directory of Black women therapists, including a listing of the type of care they specialize in (e.g., anxiety, depression, body image, LGBTQIA\\+ identity), a [podcast](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.blackfemaletherapists.com\u002Fpodcast), and a mental health blog. You can also check out [six other mental health resources](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bonappetit.com\u002Fstory\u002Fvirtual-mental-health-resources) offering virtual support to Black people—and I’m adding Lauryn Hill’s live album [*Lauryn Hill Unplugged No. 2.0*](https:\u002F\u002Fopen.spotify.com\u002Falbum\u002F22tn8fUpD1lurSga9yuqhM) because no one can tell me listening to it in the car doesn’t have special healing properties.\n\n#### Try a new type of weed (if you’re into that)\nIn hindsight, chilling in bed on my phone after trying Canndescent’s [“charge” joint](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.canndescent.com\u002Fpre-rolls) feels like a missed opportunity considering how much of an enjoyable body\u002Fmind high it provided. Maybe I should’ve had a station ready with snacks, coloring books, art activities, and tender\u002Ffunny videos? My thoughts once the high started to wane were basically, Wow, well, I guess I’m going to have to be a grown-up and start investing in quality weed now. It was easily the best high I’ve experienced from a pre-rolled joint. Canndescent offers (limited-edition) [holiday joints](https:\u002F\u002Fwww.iheartjane.com\u002Fembed\u002Fstores\u002F2219\u002Fproducts\u002F202311\u002Fcanndescent-cheer?utm_source=copy&utm_medium=organic_social&utm_campaign=product_share&utm_content=2219?blockScrollToTop) too\\! If you’re looking to broaden your weed toolbox, consider trying out [Papa & Barkley’s THC body oil](https:\u002F\u002Fpapaandbarkley.com\u002Fproduct\u002Freleaf-body-oil\u002F) for pain and tension relief. And if exploring vaginal cannabis products is of interest, [Quim’s everyday CBD (or THC) oil](https:\u002F\u002Fitsquim.com\u002Fproduct\u002Fhappy-clam\u002F) can be used for everything from menstruation relief to post-shower TLC.\n\n#### Embrace optimism and uncertainty as an act of wellness\nLately, I’ve been opening up more to the idea that positive occurrences and opportunities, as well as the roads leading to them, may not manifest in the way I envisioned in my head—and maybe that’s okay. I’ve also decided to give leaning into positive *what-ifs* a go. *What if* this isn’t working out because I’m being redirected to something that’s more aligned with who I am and what I want? *What if* there’s no need to chase or frantically grasp and that certain roadblocks are blessings in disguise? *What if* the right things, the right people, and all of the good shit will flow into your life, and the task isn’t to chase or mourn or be swallowed up by shame, but rather to learn, explore, heal, and evolve into the best *most you* version of yourself? *What if* “all of the good shit” looks nothing like you ever imagined? *What if* it’s going to be okay, even if it doesn’t feel like it, even if you can’t see or feel that light at the end of the tunnel right now? If you believed that, what would you do next? That’s the space I’ve been exploring lately, and it’s a refreshing change of pace.\n\n","articleSection":"healthyish","author":[{"@type":"Person","name":"Martine
